# 13F Institutional Ownership Database — Roadmap

Single source of truth for forward work. Updated 2026-05-01 (`conv-24-doc-sync` — fund-level cleanup arc closed: PR #242 fund-cleanup-batch + branch-cleanup chore + PR #243 saba-proshares-reclassify; predecessor: `conv-23-doc-sync`). Discipline: items live here or do not exist. Workstream-specific plans live in `docs/plans/<slug>.md` while active, archive on completion.

See `docs/findings/2026-04-25-backlog-collapse.md` for the closure rationale and KILL-list cataloguing this entry replaces.

## Current backlog (verified 2026-05-01 conv-24-doc-sync)

### P0 — Production blockers

### P1 — Active commitments

- **ui-audit-walkthrough** — 24 per-tab "Bugs (visual)" + "Completeness gaps" blank rows in `docs/ui-audit-01-triage.md` need a Serge+Claude live walkthrough. 1-2 hr; not a Code session.

### P2 — Next sprint

- ~~**cef-residual-cleanup**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-02.** PR-A `cef-residual-cleanup-adx` (#250, squash `adb1ba9`) flipped 96 ADX byte-identical duplicates; PR-B `cef-asa-flip-and-relabel` (squash `<TBD>`) flipped + relabeled 350 ASA UNKNOWN rows / $1.752B to `SYN_0001230869`. Global `series_id='UNKNOWN' AND is_latest=TRUE` 446 → 0. See COMPLETED table.
- **fund-structure-column** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #249 cef-scoping). Add `fund_structure` enum column to `fund_universe` ({`open_end`, `closed_end`, `etf`, `bdc`, `interval`}) — orthogonal to `fund_strategy`. Currently structure is inferred indirectly via `series_id` prefix (SYN_ = CEF-or-open-end ambiguous, real SEC series_id = open-end), which is fragile. Lets `cross.py` and display layer make structure-aware decisions (e.g., NAV premium/discount only for `closed_end`). Workstream: investigation PR (schema design + downstream impact) → backfill PR (populate from SEC form-type signals) → display integration PR. Blockers: must follow `cef-residual-cleanup` (depends on clean SYN_ state); source-of-truth question (SEC form-type vs prospectus vs holdings shape); interaction with `fund-strategy-taxonomy-finalization`. Full spec at [§ fund-structure-column](#fund-structure-column).
- **parent-level-display-canonical-reads** — Migrate the 18 parent-level display read sites from `holdings_v2.manager_type` and `holdings_v2.entity_type` (legacy/derived) to canonical `entity_classification_history.classification` / `entity_current.classification`. Includes fix for `query4` silent-drop bug ([register.py:746-750](scripts/queries/register.py:746)) where rows with disagreeing `manager_type` and `entity_type` fall to "Other/Unknown". Tracked as the institution-level half of the consolidation sequence (separate from fund-level, which closed with PR-1d on 2026-05-01). Decision D4 from the PR-1c audit applies: always read canonical when migrated; precedence rule for managers without an `entity_classification_history` row to be defined as part of this work. Surfaced 2026-05-01 (PR-1d follow-up). **Scoping investigation (2026-05-02):** see `docs/findings/institution_scoping.md` for full PR sequencing, Q1 cycle interaction, and 12 open questions. Critical-path subset = 5 PRs (`inst-eid-bridge-investigation`, `ingestion-manifest-reconcile`, `query4-fix-option-a`, `inst-eid-bridge-fix`, this item). Total estimated session count for the full institution-level sequence ≈ 14 sessions. Synthesis-promoted blocker: cross-tier brand-vs-filer entity_id duplication exposes ~$27.8T of fund-side AUM as invisible in any institution-coverage Admin Refresh view.
- **inst-eid-bridge** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (`institution-scoping`). Bridge the brand-vs-filer entity_id duplication. 1,225–1,326 institutions receive fund rollups but have zero `is_latest=TRUE` rows in `holdings_v2` because fund-tier rolls up to "brand" eids (e.g. Vanguard `eid=1`, PIMCO `eid=30`) while institution-tier 13F filings live on filer-CIK eids (e.g. Vanguard `eid=4375`). Top exposure: VOYA $2,714B, Vanguard Group $2,541B, PIMCO $1,716B, TEACHERS ADVISORS $1,571B, TRANSAMERICA $1,303B (full top-25 in scoping doc). Two-PR workstream: investigation PR (read-only manifest of all 1,225 invisible institutions × proposed bridge mappings via `entity_relationships`), then population PR (entity_relationships + fund-side rollup re-pointing). Q1 2026 cycle (~2026-05-15) may surface new duplicates; investigation can ship pre-cycle, population PR ships post-cycle. Sized: investigation S, population L. Critical path for Admin Refresh System institution-coverage view. **Critical-path sequencing (added post-PR #252):** Wave 1 (parallel) — CP-1 `inst-eid-bridge-investigation` (read-only audit) + CP-3 `query4-fix-option-a` (10-line CASE rewrite at [register.py:746-750](scripts/queries/register.py:746)). Wave 2 — CP-2 `ingestion-manifest-reconcile` (depends on CP-1). Wave 3 — CP-4 `inst-eid-bridge-fix` (depends on CP-1 + CP-2; bundles `deprecated-fund-rollup-targets-cleanup`). Wave 4 — CP-5 `parent-level-display-canonical-reads` (depends on CP-4; resolves `classification-join-utility-resolution` decision). **Manual review gate:** a separate chat decision must precede CP-4 execution — CP-1 investigation output goes to chat for review before the CP-4 prompt is written. Blast radius (1,225+ institutions, $27.8T fund-side AUM) is too large for inferred scope. **Decisions doc (added 2026-05-02):** `docs/decisions/inst_eid_bridge_decisions.md` locks the three BLOCKER resolutions from PR #254 §9. **CP-4 split per decisions doc:** CP-4a `inst-eid-bridge-fix-aliases` (S, pre-cycle): ~5 BRAND_TO_FILER merges (Vanguard, PIMCO, small aliases). CP-4b `inst-eid-bridge-author-top25` (M, pre-cycle): ~25 AUTHOR_NEW_BRIDGE writes for hv2-counterparty-discoverable brands. CP-4c `inst-eid-bridge-author-next75` (M, post-cycle): ~75 AUTHOR_NEW_BRIDGE writes via ADV-first + manual pairing. **CP-5 dependency:** requires CP-4a + CP-4b minimum (~$24T of $27.8T bridged) for read sweep payoff. CP-4c parallelizable.
- **pimco-13f-ingestion-gap** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #254 `inst-eid-bridge-investigation` §7.2). Priority: P2. **Problem.** PIMCO does not file 13F under any entity present in `holdings_v2`. CIK `0001163368` (PACIFIC INVESTMENT MANAGEMENT CO LLC, `eid=2322`) is the canonical PIMCO US adviser registration but is absent from `holdings_v2.cik` entirely. `eid=30` (PIMCO name-only) and `eid=2322` both carry $0 filer AUM. Allianz parent entities (`eid=1358`, `eid=589`) carry filer AUM but the totals ($20.4B + $348.4B) cannot account for PIMCO's expected $1.7T US equity rollup. **Diagnosis hypotheses:** (1) form-13F-NT filtering excludes PIMCO's filings during ingestion; (2) Allianz parent-rollup logic absorbs PIMCO filings into a parent eid; (3) known-broken filer pattern in `load_13f_v2.py`. **Workstream:** investigation-first, fix-second. Investigation PR (S) — read SEC EDGAR for PIMCO 13F filings, cross-reference against `load_13f_v2.py` ingestion logic, identify why PIMCO CIK is absent. Fix PR (sized after investigation). **Out of scope:** brand-vs-filer bridge for `eid=30` → `eid=2322` (handled by CP-4a per `inst_eid_bridge_decisions.md`).
- **fund-strategy-taxonomy-finalization** — Surfaced 2026-05-01 (PR-4 follow-up). Review and finalize the five edge categories in the canonical `fund_strategy` taxonomy. Several values were inherited from the original classifier and carry vague labels or arbitrary boundaries that do not survive scrutiny: (1) **`balanced`** (60-90% equity composition) — vague label, boundary with `multi_asset` is arbitrary; decide keep as composition-based bucket / rename to `active_equity_heavy` / merge into `active`; (2) **`multi_asset`** (30-60% equity composition) — boundaries with `balanced` (60%) and `bond_or_other` (30%) are both arbitrary thresholds; decide keep distinct / merge with `balanced` / rename; (3) **`bond_or_other`** — heterogeneous bucket; the `saba-proshares-reclassify` 2026-05-01 PR moved 39 ProShares short / inverse / leveraged-short funds out of this bucket to `passive` (closing the bucket's largest miscategorisation); residual is bond funds + niche cases. Could still split into `bond` and `inverse_or_short` if a richer taxonomy is preferred — but the urgency is gone now that ProShares is corrected; (4) **`excluded`** — combines money markets, fund-of-funds, and ETF wrappers that skip classification; should split into specific reasons; (5) **`final_filing`** — status flag, not a strategy; 12+ funds (the 12 BlackRock muni trusts, all confirmed merged Feb 2026 by the `fund-cleanup-batch` 2026-05-01 audit, plus other final-filing rows); decide whether this belongs in `fund_strategy` at all or should become a separate `is_terminating` boolean. Output: findings doc with row counts per category, decisions list, recommended target taxonomy. Trigger: orphan/NULL data is now on the table (`fund-cleanup-batch` 2026-05-01 audit closed `canonical-value-coverage-audit`); residual orphan disposition tracked under `fund-holdings-orphan-investigation` and `historical-fund-holdings-drift-audit`. The merge/split decisions can now be staged.
- **canonical-value-coverage-audit** — broader audit of NULL `fund_strategy`, orphan series, edge cohorts (UNKNOWN orphans / SYN drifters / BlackRock muni trusts), 3-way `CASE` NULL semantics in `cross.py`, and rows where `fund_holdings_v2.fund_strategy_at_filing` differs from `fund_universe.fund_strategy`. **Status (2026-05-01 conv-24):** Phase 1 (data-pull / row-count + AUM exposure across canonical buckets) was executed inside `fund-cleanup-batch` (PR #242); see `docs/findings/fund_cleanup_batch_results.md` §1a–§1h. The structured per-bucket count + AUM exposure + recommended treatment table is the still-open deliverable; the SYN drift cohort + 301-series orphan cohort + 3-way CASE NULL semantics review remain to be characterized end-to-end. Trigger: next architectural session that picks up `fund-strategy-taxonomy-finalization`.
- **index-benchmark-validation** — Systematize fund-to-index classification using N-PORT holdings data. Builds on the one-off Item 8 work from 2026-04-09 (existing `index_proxies` / `fund_index_scores` / `benchmark_weights` tables) by turning it into a maintained pipeline. Coverage findings: `docs/findings/index_benchmark_coverage.md`. **Phase 1 — Index reference table:** 27 benchmarks identified from `fund_universe` naming (S&P 500: 227 funds / $4.0T; Total Stock Market: 14 / $2.7T; Nasdaq 100: 98 / $579B; plus sector + international). Pick one representative fund per benchmark as the reference portfolio (e.g. Vanguard 500 Index for S&P 500). Store as `benchmark_portfolios(benchmark_name, series_id, quarter, ticker, weight)` — supersedes `index_proxies` once parity verified. **Phase 2 — Correlation scoring pipeline:** for each fund in `fund_holdings_v2`, compute overlap % and weight correlation against each benchmark. Store as `fund_index_correlation(series_id, benchmark_name, quarter, overlap_pct, weight_corr)` — supersedes `fund_index_scores`. Rules: >90% overlap + >0.95 weight corr ⇒ confirmed passive; <60% overlap ⇒ confirmed active; middle ⇒ review. **Phase 3 — Unmatched fund classification:** 3,599 funds with "Index"/"ETF" in name ($4.6T) remain unmatched to a specific benchmark; correlation against the reference portfolios will classify them. Periodic weight validation against external sources (S&P factsheets). **Phase 4 — Sector fund integration:** 11 GICS sector benchmarks identified (Tech $151B, Health Care $63B, Financials $70B, Energy $49B, etc.); incorporate sector fund compositions into Sector Rotation tab. Priority: Medium. Prerequisite: none. Depends on: N-PORT data (available). Blocks: improved active/passive accuracy on all tabs.
- **register-active-universe-consistency** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #252 `institution-scoping`). The Register tab applies four different "active" predicates across read sites: [register.py:1018](scripts/queries/register.py:1018) excludes activists from the active universe; [register.py:472](scripts/queries/register.py:472), [register.py:1354](scripts/queries/register.py:1354), and [market.py:373/498](scripts/queries/market.py:373) include them. Same tab, same conceptual filter, four different SQL predicates — active-universe size depends on which endpoint a UI element calls. Two-PR workstream: investigation PR (S, confirm the four sites, document the intended canonical definition, surface any other read sites with the same shape) → fix PR (S, single canonical helper, all four sites migrate to it, no data writes). **Sequencing: must ship BEFORE any activist-as-flag refactor** — the flag refactor depends on a single canonical active-universe definition existing first. Out of scope: the activist-as-flag schema migration itself (separate workstream from PR #252 Phase 5).

### P3 — Quick wins / low priority

- **source-type-value-canonicalization** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #255 `ingestion-manifest-reconcile` Appendix A §A.5; entry confirmed in CP-4a chat 2026-05-02). `ingestion_manifest.source_type` writes use two different value conventions: direct writes (e.g. legacy paths) emit `'NPORT'` while SourcePipeline-base writes emit `'nport_holdings'` (sourced from `PIPELINE_CADENCE.keys()` in `scripts/pipeline/`). The mismatch affects `admin_bp.py:1346` last-run lookup — admin dashboard last-run cards may miss a recent run if the lookup keys on one convention but the most recent write used the other. Workstream: audit all `source_type` writes to enumerate the two conventions, decide canonical value per pipeline (likely `'nport_holdings'` for the SourcePipeline-aligned set, plus a one-time UPDATE to backfill any direct writes onto the canonical convention), patch any remaining direct-write call sites, then update `admin_bp.py:1346` lookup. Single S PR. Parallel to critical path (no dependency on `inst-eid-bridge` or `parent-level-display-canonical-reads`). Out of scope for the original CP-2 PR per the bias-toward-DROP rule (scope was schema-name reconcile, not value-name reconcile).
- **v2-loader-is-latest-watchpoint** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #247 close-out; Open Question #4 in PR #246 attribution doc). Watchpoint, not a code change. After Q1 2026 13F cycle (~2026-05-15) re-run `audit_unknown_inventory.py`; expected residual = 446 rows (the deferred CEF cohort). Residual > 446 ⇒ Apr-15 v2 loader bug recurred ⇒ open `v2-loader-is-latest-fix` PR. Residual = 446 ⇒ close Open Question #4 as resolved-by-evidence. Full spec at [§ v2-loader-is-latest-watchpoint](#v2-loader-is-latest-watchpoint).
- **retired-loader-residue-watchpoint** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #249 cef-scoping). Watchpoint, not a code change. PR #249 found that 446 UNKNOWN rows in `fund_holdings_v2` came from `scripts/retired/fetch_nport.py`, the only literal-`UNKNOWN` write site in the repo. Loader is retired. After PR-B (`cef-asa-flip-and-relabel`) lands AND after Q1 2026 13F cycle runs (~2026-05-15, post-Stage 5 DROP): re-run `audit_unknown_inventory.py`. Expected residual: 0. Residual > 0 ⇒ either retired-loader residue not fully cleaned (re-run cleanup) or a new write site introduced the literal-`UNKNOWN` pattern (grep `pipeline/`, then targeted fix PR). Full spec at [§ retired-loader-residue-watchpoint](#retired-loader-residue-watchpoint).
- **asa-2025-11-syn-source-investigation** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (`cef_asa_prep_investigation.md`, commit `79350a5`). ASA's existing 2025-11 `SYN_0001230869` row sources from accession `0001049169-26-000039` — Donnelley filing agent, not ASA's own NPORT-P. Out of scope for PR-B (`cef-asa-flip-and-relabel`). Investigate whether `SYN_` rows should source canonical NPORT-P filings only, or whether filing-agent surrogates are acceptable in the canonical path; if unacceptable, scope a separate cleanup PR. Full spec at [§ asa-2025-11-syn-source-investigation](#asa-2025-11-syn-source-investigation).
- **ingestion-manifest-coverage-watchpoint** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (`cef_asa_prep_investigation.md`, commit `79350a5`). Watchpoint, not a code change. ASA's UNKNOWN-side accessions are not registered in `ingestion_manifest` — the legacy synth path wrote `fund_holdings_v2` rows without manifest entries. After PR-B (`cef-asa-flip-and-relabel`) closes: audit `ingestion_manifest` for any other CIKs with `fund_holdings_v2` rows but no manifest entry. Should be empty if PR-B logic is correct. Full spec at [§ ingestion-manifest-coverage-watchpoint](#ingestion-manifest-coverage-watchpoint).
- **stage-b-turnover-deferred-funds** — Three Vanguard funds and similar individual cases are passive in behavior but their names do not match systemic INDEX_PATTERNS rules: Vanguard Primecap (~$76B), Vanguard Windsor II (~$65B), Vanguard Equity Income (~$62B). These will be flagged for reclassification by Stage B (position turnover detection) which validates passive behavior via holdings stability rather than name regex. Total ~$203B AUM affected. Adjacent case: Bridgeway Ultra-Small Company Market (~$0.13B) — passive Bridgeway-internal index tracker that the PR-2 sweep deliberately did not catch (the `\bUltra\b` pattern was rejected because of false positives on actively-managed Ultra-named funds, and `\bBridgeway\b` is mixed-purpose). Surfaced 2026-05-01 (PR-2 follow-up); demoted from P2 → P3 in `conv-24-doc-sync` because the trigger (Stage B turnover detection design) is itself a separate, larger initiative not yet on this roadmap. Trigger: Stage B turnover detection design.
- **per-fund-deferred-decisions** — Five named funds surfaced for chat decision but deliberately not reclassified by PR #242 (`fund-cleanup-batch`) or PR #243 (`saba-proshares-reclassify`); each needs its own per-fund review or a loader-gap fix before any UPDATE: (1) Eaton Vance Tax-Advantaged Dividend Income + 2 NEW global variants — all currently `balanced`, decision is whether prospectus-level review supports `balanced` vs `bond_or_other`; (2) Calamos Global Total Return Fund (1,412 orphan holdings rows in `fund_holdings_v2`, no `fund_universe` row at all — loader gap, not a classification call); (3) the 96-row N/A cohort (rows where `fund_name` is literally `'N/A'` in `fund_holdings_v2`, also no `fund_universe` row — loader gap). Surfaced 2026-05-01 fund-cleanup-batch §4d. Trigger: next per-fund review session, or whenever the loader gap for Calamos/N/A is investigated as part of `fund-holdings-orphan-investigation`.
- **historical-fund-holdings-drift-audit** — Surfaced 2026-05-01 (fund-cleanup-batch §1g). 31,400 non-SYN holdings rows where `fund_holdings_v2.fund_strategy_at_filing` disagrees with `fund_universe.fund_strategy` (40,843 total minus the 9,405 documented SYN drifters from PR-1a §2.3). Same shape as the SYN drift cohort but a larger non-SYN cohort. Drift is harmless at runtime — PR-4's JOIN architectural fix in `compute_peer_rotation.py:421-449` serves canonical via `LEFT JOIN fund_universe`; the snapshot column is preserved by design as `fund_strategy_at_filing` (snapshot semantics, intentional). Audit characterizes the historical drift class for future remediation. See `docs/findings/fund_cleanup_batch_results.md` §1g.
- **D10 Admin UI for `entity_identifiers_staging`** — moved here from Deferred 2026-04-27 (roadmap-priority-moves). Trigger ("next admin UI iteration") not yet fired; activated to surface the 280-row staging backlog for review before the Q1 2026 cycle (~2026-05-15).
- **Tier 4 unmatched classifications (427)** — surfaced 2026-04-28 (calamos-merge-tier4-classify). The Tier 4 keyword sweep classified 230 of 657 bootstrap_tier4 entities (1 passive `Index` + 229 active across `Income Fund` / `Municipal` / `Closed-End` / `Interval`); the remaining 427 still carry `classification='unknown'` because their canonical names contain none of the spec keywords. Sample (10 random) shows 100% are CEFs / interval funds / private credit funds (`John Hancock Income Securities Trust`, `Western Asset High Income Opportunity Fund`, `BlackRock MuniYield NY`, `Eagle Point Defensive Income Trust`, `NB Crossroads Private Markets`, etc.) — strongly biased active. Trigger: next entity-curation pass willing to expand the keyword set (`Trust`, `MuniYield`, `Private`, `Opportunity`, `High Yield`, ADV-anchored CEF lookup) or do per-entity manual sign-off. NAV exposure is bounded by Tier 4 cohort size ($566.7B across 657 / 230 = 427 unmatched ≈ $370B max).
- **unmerged-branch-decisions (2)** — surfaced 2026-05-01 (branch-cleanup). Two local branches retained because their PRs were closed without merge. **Chat decision (`conv-24-doc-sync`): both flagged DELETE.** (1) `claude/reverent-kirch-c1fcdf` (PR [#172](https://github.com/sergetismen/13f-ownership/pull/172) CLOSED) — DM13-D/E discovery branch; actual fix shipped under [#173](https://github.com/sergetismen/13f-ownership/pull/173) so discovery work is captured. (2) `ui-audit-01` (PR [#107](https://github.com/sergetismen/13f-ownership/pull/107) CLOSED) — feeds the active P1 `ui-audit-walkthrough` item via `docs/ui-audit-01-triage.md`; the triage doc is on `main` and is what the live walkthrough consumes, so the branch tip is no longer load-bearing. Both can be deleted in the next housekeeping pass; no per-branch spot-check required given the chat decision. See `docs/findings/branch_cleanup_audit.md` Phase 3.
- **drop-multi-strategy-bucket** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #252 `institution-scoping`). `manager_type='multi_strategy'` contains 2 CIKs / $11.7B: Adams Diversified Equity Fund (a CEF, not a hedge fund) and Diversified Management Inc. Neither is a multi-strategy pod-shop; the actual pod-shops (Citadel, Millennium, Point72, Balyasny) live in `manager_type='hedge_fund'`. The bucket is misnamed and substantively empty. Per PR #252 Phase 2 recommendation: drop the bucket entirely (Option B); reclassify Adams to `closed_end` (CEF — pending the `fund-structure-column` workstream) and Diversified Management Inc per its actual filing pattern. Single S PR — reclassify 2 CIKs, drop bucket from canonical taxonomy. Sequencing: parallel to critical path; can ship anytime. No dependency on `inst-eid-bridge` work.
- **classification-join-utility-resolution** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #252 `institution-scoping`). [queries_helpers.py:171](scripts/queries_helpers.py:171) contains `classification_join` — a canonical `entity_classification_history`-aware JOIN macro with **zero callers**. Either dead code (delete) or the canonical helper for `parent-level-display-canonical-reads` (adopt during CP-5). Decision deferred to CP-5: if CP-5 adopts `classification_join`, keep, document, and expand test coverage; if CP-5 builds a different canonical helper, delete `classification_join` in the same PR to prevent dead-code resurrection. No standalone PR — resolution rides on CP-5.
- **deprecated-fund-rollup-targets-cleanup** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #252 `institution-scoping`). 19 fund-rollup-target entities are deprecated in `entity_classification_history` with $68.7B exposed. Successor eids were created during the Apr 11–12 entity-merge marathon, but fund-tier rollups (`fund_universe.dm_rollup_entity_id` and `fund_holdings_v2.dm_rollup_entity_id`) were not re-pointed. **Decision: bundle into CP-4 (`inst-eid-bridge-fix`).** The bridge fix already re-points fund-tier rollups; adding 19 deprecated-target re-points to the same transaction is the cleanest rollback boundary, and CP-4's Phase 1 re-validation already needs to confirm ECH state. If CP-4 scope grows beyond manageable, split into a CP-4b follow-up; decision made when the CP-4 prompt is written.
- **inst-eid-bridge-orphan-triage** — Surfaced 2026-05-02 (PR #254 `inst-eid-bridge-investigation` §4.4). Priority: P3. **Problem.** 723 BRAND_ORPHAN brands carry $943B fund-side AUM with no bridging signal: no `entity_relationships` row, no name match to a holdings_v2 filer, no CIK overlap. 656 (90%) created via `bootstrap_tier4` cohort/wave processes; small-dollar long tail (avg $1.3B per brand). **Decision** per `inst_eid_bridge_decisions.md`: defer per-brand triage. Effort is high, AUM is low. Ship only if a triggering display gap surfaces post-CP-5 (e.g., a tab specifically showing brand-side rollups that exposes the orphan visibility issue). **Workstream:** per-brand triage if triggered. Each brand resolves to one of: merge into a filer eid (BRAND_TO_FILER), close as inactive shell, or accept as fund-only attribution. **Out of scope:** 31 `entity_type='fund'` orphans (handled by `fund-holdings-orphan-investigation` P2).

| Auto-refresh scheduler (cron) | First time auto-refresh would have prevented an issue |

---

## Known issues

- ~~**fund_strategy classification drift**~~ — RESOLVED 2026-05-01 by the PR-2 / PR-4 sequence. (1) PR-2 added the pipeline write-path lock (`_apply_fund_strategy_lock` + `_upsert_fund_universe` COALESCE in [scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py](scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py)); once a series carries a non-NULL `fund_strategy`, subsequent classifier outputs are discarded. (2) PR-4 changed the only remaining query-layer reader of point-in-time holdings (`compute_peer_rotation.py:_materialize_fund_agg`) to LEFT JOIN `fund_universe.fund_strategy` instead of reading `fund_holdings_v2.fund_strategy_at_filing` (column renamed in the same PR). With both legs landed the per-quarter drift class is structurally impossible. The historical mismatch between `fund_universe.fund_strategy` and `fund_holdings_v2.fund_strategy_at_filing` is preserved in the `_at_filing` column (snapshot semantics, intentional) and was quantified 2026-05-01 by the `fund-cleanup-batch` audit (40,843 latest-only divergent rows; see `docs/findings/fund_cleanup_batch_results.md` §1g). Residual non-SYN drift (~31,400 rows) carried as P3 `historical-fund-holdings-drift-audit`.

## cef-residual-cleanup

**Status:** **CLOSED 2026-05-02** · **Priority:** P2 · **Surfaced:** PR [#247](https://github.com/ST5555-Code/Institutional-Ownership/pull/247) (BRANCH 2 holdouts) · **Reframed:** PR [#249](https://github.com/ST5555-Code/Institutional-Ownership/pull/249) (cef-scoping) · **Closed:** PR-A #250 + PR-B `cef-asa-flip-and-relabel`

**Problem.** 446 rows / $4.741B in `fund_holdings_v2` under `series_id='UNKNOWN'` from 2 CEF CIKs (Adams Diversified Equity Fund `0000002230`, ASA Gold & Precious Metals `0001230869`). Per PR #249 scoping: this is migration-015 residue from the retired loader `scripts/retired/fetch_nport.py`, NOT a CEF architecture gap. CEFs file N-PORT under Rule 30b1-9 and the `SYN_<cik>` namespace already correctly loads 436 of 438 CEFs in `fund_holdings_v2` ($625.94B AUM).

Decision per PR #249: keep `SYN_<cik>` as canonical CEF identifier (Option C — status quo). Skip historical N-CSR backfill (Parser Option D). Net new modern data over N-PORT = 0; ~3–5 weeks effort if ever pursued. Original 4-PR follow-on arc (cef-fetch-pipeline, cef-parser, cef-holdings-load, display integration) DROPPED.

### Workstream sequence (revised, ~1–2 sessions)

- ~~**PR-A `cef-residual-cleanup-adx`** (S) — flip 96 ADX byte-identical duplicates to `is_latest=FALSE`.~~ **Landed 2026-05-02.** Single-period cohort (2025-09-30); 96/96 byte-identical to `SYN_0000002230` companions; 0 mismatches; 0 orphans. Global `series_id='UNKNOWN' AND is_latest=TRUE` 446 → 350.
- ~~**PR-B `cef-asa-flip-and-relabel`** (S) — flip 350 ASA UNKNOWN rows to `is_latest=FALSE` and relabel to `series_id='SYN_0001230869'`.~~ **Landed 2026-05-02.** 350/350 byte-identical to ASA's N-PORT filings ($0.00 per-period delta); single-tx INSERT 350 SYN + UPDATE 350 UNKNOWN; AUM conservation Δ = $0.00. Fund-attribution override (entity_id 11278 → 26793, dm_rollup_name 'Calamos Investments' → 'ASA Gold and Precious Metals LTD Fund') applied per chat decision; mirrors existing 2025-11 SYN row. Global `series_id='UNKNOWN' AND is_latest=TRUE` 350 → 0. Workstream closes.

### Out of scope

- N-CSR / NSAR holdings parsing (resolved by PR #249: not needed).
- BDC (Form 10-K), interval funds — separate workstreams.

### Revision history

- **2026-05-02** — PR-B reframed from `cef-asa-period-backfill` (M, fetch+load+flip) to `cef-asa-flip-and-relabel` (S, flip+relabel) per `docs/findings/cef_asa_prep_investigation.md` (commit `79350a5`). Investigation found ASA UNKNOWN rows are byte-identical ($0.00 delta) to the corresponding NPORT-P filings already on EDGAR, so the data is already in `fund_holdings_v2` — only the `series_id` label is wrong. v2 loader rerun would create rows under `1230869_<accession>` (CEFs report `series_id=None`), inconsistent with the existing 2025-11 `SYN_0001230869` row.

## fund-structure-column

**Status:** Open · **Priority:** P2 · **Surfaced:** PR [#249](https://github.com/ST5555-Code/Institutional-Ownership/pull/249) (cef-scoping)

**Problem.** `fund_universe.fund_strategy` describes investment style (active, passive, etc.) but does not capture fund structure. CEFs trade at premium/discount to NAV; open-end funds do not. ETFs, BDCs, and interval funds each behave differently in display layer. Currently structure is inferred indirectly via `series_id` prefix (`SYN_` = CEF-or-open-end ambiguous, real SEC `series_id` = open-end), which is fragile.

**Proposal.** Add `fund_structure` enum column to `fund_universe`: `{open_end, closed_end, etf, bdc, interval}`. Orthogonal to `fund_strategy`. Lets `cross.py` and display layer make structure-aware decisions (e.g., show NAV premium/discount only for `closed_end`).

### Workstream shape (estimated)

- **Investigation PR** — schema design, migration plan, downstream query impact analysis.
- **Backfill PR** — populate `fund_structure` for all existing `fund_universe` rows from SEC form-type signals.
- **Display integration PR** — surface in relevant tabs.

### Blockers

- Must follow `cef-residual-cleanup` (depends on clean `SYN_` state).
- Source-of-truth question: SEC form-type, fund prospectus, or derived from holdings shape?
- Interaction with `fund-strategy-taxonomy-finalization` (separate P2 workstream).

**Out of scope:** `nav_per_share` enrichment (deferred — no current analytic depends on it).

| 2026-05-01 | **classifier-name-patterns (PR-2)** | Extended `INDEX_PATTERNS` in [scripts/pipeline/nport_parsers.py:38](scripts/pipeline/nport_parsers.py:38) with eight new alternations on top of the original keyword set: `qqq`, `target\s*retirement`, `target\s*date`, `\d+(?:\.\d+)?x` (leveraged-multiplier digits like 2X / 3X / 1.5X), `proshares`, `profund`, `direxion`, `daily\s*inverse`, `inverse`. The original plan's `\bUltra\b` / `\bUltraPro\b` patterns were rejected after the dry-run revealed 4 false positives on actively-managed Ultra-named funds (American Century Ultra, LVIP American Century Ultra, Wasatch Ultra Growth, Bridgeway Ultra-Small Company); replaced with `\bproshares\b` since ProShares Trust is exclusively a passive / leveraged-ETF family. **Phase 2 — pipeline write-path lock** in [scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py](scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py): new `_apply_fund_strategy_lock(prod_con, series_touched)` (pre-promote helper that reads prod `fund_universe.fund_strategy`/`fund_category` and rewrites staged `fund_holdings_v2` + `stg_nport_fund_universe` rows to the prod values for any series whose prod row carries non-NULL `fund_strategy`) plus a COALESCE safety net inside `_upsert_fund_universe` (uses `COALESCE(prior_fund_strategy, staged.fund_strategy)` so even if the lock helper is bypassed the prod values still win). Three-branch semantics: new series → write classifier output; existing with non-null `fund_strategy` → preserve; existing with NULL → write classifier output (backfill case). | 2026-04-30 | **sr-fund-quarter-filter (PR #215)** | Two enhancements to Sector Rotation Fund view. New `GET /api/v1/fund_quarter_completeness` returns per-quarter `months_available` + `complete` flag (true iff 3 N-PORT report-months filed) from `fund_holdings_v2`; tab fetches once on mount and filters out incomplete destination quarters from the sector heatmap when `level='fund'`. Institution view + the static Net Flows heatmap unaffected. New `GET /api/v1/sector_monthly_flows?sector=&quarter=` computes monthly net flows from paired filers (funds present in both current and prior month); months are derived from data because N-PORT report-months trail the filing quarter by one period (quarter='2026Q1' contains report_months 2025-10/11/12); funds present in only one month are excluded since most filers report only at quarter-end and treating a missing month as an exit produced spurious trillion-dollar swings. Heatmap tooltip lazy-fetches per (sector, quarter), caches in component state, shows "Loading monthly detail…" while in-flight, renders abbreviated month labels in JetBrains Mono with green/red semantic colors per DarkStyle.md. Squash commit lands on `main`. |

Distinguishing-axis breakdown: `payoff_profile` resolves only 397 / 1,551 NPORT_NORMAL groups (25.6%); 1,154 (74.4%) have multiple positions on the same payoff side. The actual PK is the surrogate `row_id BIGINT` (already enforced via `fund_holdings_v2_row_id_pkey` in migration `020_pk_enforcement.py`); `(series_id, report_month, accession_number, cusip)` was never a natural key. **No fix.** Recommendation: (a) note in PK-assumption docs that this tuple is non-unique; (b) analytic dedup uses `SUM(shares_or_principal)` / `SUM(market_value_usd)` across the group, optionally filtered by `payoff_profile='Long'` — already the convention in current rollup queries; (c) future N-PORT line-item ordinal column is non-blocking. Findings doc: `docs/findings/inf53-backfill-mig015-multirow.md`. No DB writes, no schema changes. |

Per-table flow: drop user indexes; rebuild table with surviving columns + original `nextval('<table>_row_id_seq')` default + `PRIMARY KEY (row_id)`; `INSERT INTO …_new SELECT … FROM …` (12,270,984 holdings_v2 rows + 14,568,775 fund_holdings_v2 rows); `DROP TABLE`; `RENAME`; recreate all indexes. End-to-end on prod 25 GB DB: 38s wall (372% CPU). Schema versions stamped `022_drop_redundant_v2_columns`. Writer cleanups co-shipped: `scripts/load_13f_v2.py` (staging DDL `_STG_HOLDINGS_V2_DDL`, `_TARGET_TABLE_COLUMNS` tuple, `INSERT INTO holdings_v2` column list and SELECT body), `scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py` (`_TARGET_TABLE_COLUMNS` — auto-propagates to `_STG_TARGET_DDL` and `tests/pipeline/test_load_nport.py:DDL_FUND_HOLDINGS_V2`; `INSERT INTO fund_holdings_v2 / SELECT … FROM stg_nport_holdings`), `tests/pipeline/test_load_13f_v2.py:DDL_HOLDINGS_V2`. **Verification:** schema check (3 cols ABSENT, int-23 cols still present); dev server on :8001 reloaded; AAPL + EQT smoke-tested across 8 endpoints — `query1` (Register, 104 / 85 rows), `portfolio_context` (Conviction, no error), `fund_portfolio_managers` (50 rows), `peer_rotation` (Sector Rotation, full payload), `sector_flows`, `smart_money`, `flow_analysis`, `holder_momentum` — all 200, zero exceptions in app log. `npm run build` clean (1089 modules, all tabs bundled, 1.58s). `pre-commit` clean (ruff, pylint, bandit). `validate_entities.py --prod` 7 PASS / 1 FAIL / 8 MANUAL (sole FAIL `wellington_sub_advisory` is the documented baseline; `total_aum` PASS at 0.0% diff confirming no row-level data loss). `pytest tests/` 364 passed. |

Discovery against `fund_holdings_v2`: 14,568,843 total rows, 9,037,397 distinct `(series_id, report_month, accession_number, cusip)` keys, 5,531,375 apparent "duplicates". The original premise (1.36M trivial dupes safe to drop via `DISTINCT ON ... ORDER BY loaded_at DESC`) was wrong. Per-group classification (`COUNT(*) > 1` AND `COUNT(DISTINCT(<all 24 non-key cols>))` against `fund_cik` / `fund_name` / `family_name` / `quarter` / `report_date` / `isin` / `issuer_name` / `ticker` / `asset_category` / `shares_or_principal` / `market_value_usd` / `pct_of_nav` / `fair_value_level` / `is_restricted` / `payoff_profile` / `fund_strategy` / `best_index` / `entity_id` / `rollup_entity_id` / `dm_entity_id` / `dm_rollup_entity_id` / `dm_rollup_name` / `is_latest` / `backfill_quality`): only **64 groups / 68 rows** are true row-level duplicates (every non-key column identical except `loaded_at` and `row_id`); the remaining **55,924 groups / 5,587,231 rows** are value-divergent — same key, different shares/value/pct — which the dedup spec explicitly carves out as "keep both and flag for manual review". 5.50M of the divergent rows have placeholder CUSIPs (`000000000`, `N/A`, `NULL`); 84,985 have real CUSIPs (multiple lots of the same security). Source breakdown of dup groups: 54,437 from `BACKFILL_MIG015_*` accessions, 1,551 from real N-PORT filings. Inventory CSVs written to `data/reports/inf51/`: `true_duplicate_groups_20260427_192000.csv` (64 groups, 4.4 KB) and `value_divergent_groups_20260427_192000.csv` (55,924 groups, 5.2 MB — fed into INF53). **Action taken:** trivial single DELETE of the 68 true-duplicate rows via ROW_NUMBER() partitioned by the dedup key (keep most recent `loaded_at`, lowest `row_id` as tiebreaker) restricted to groups with all-non-key-cols-identical; aggregates unchanged because each removed row is byte-identical to the kept row. The DROP TABLE / RENAME approach from the original plan was rejected as overkill (would have rewritten a 14.5M row table to remove 68 rows, and would have erased the 5.59M legitimate divergent positions). `is_latest` flags untouched (71 `is_latest=False` rows pre-existed; unchanged). `validate_entities.py` PASS=7 / FAIL=2 / MANUAL=7 — both FAILs (`wellington_sub_advisory`, `phase3_resolution_rate`) pre-existing and structurally unrelated to a 68-row holdings delete; `total_aum` and `row_count` both PASS. Post-DELETE row count 14,568,775 (delta exactly 68); `data/13f_readonly.duckdb` rebuilt via `scripts/refresh_snapshot.sh` (DuckDB `COPY FROM DATABASE`, 7.7 GB / 368 tables); app restarted on :8001. Spot check 5 tickers via `/api/v1/summary`: AAPL ($2.60T / 5928 holders), NVDA ($3.48T / 5642), MSFT ($2.69T / 6119), GOOG ($1.14T / 5015), DVN ($23.86B / 1115) — all latest_quarter=2025Q4, all HTTP 200 in <300ms. **Logged the BACKFILL_MIG015 multi-row pattern as INF53 in P3.** No schema changes, no migration, no further dedup performed. |
| 2026-04-27 | **inf50-52-nport-pipeline-fixes** | Code-only hardening of `scripts/pipeline/load_nport.py` for the two pipeline bugs surfaced during 2026-04-27 `nport-refresh-catchup` (logged as INF52 in P2 + as an unnumbered observation for the silent cleanup). **INF50 — `_cleanup_staging` silent failure.** Prior implementation called `super()._cleanup_staging(run_id)` (which DROPped `fund_holdings_v2` typed staging in its own connection), then opened a SECOND staging writer to DROP `stg_nport_holdings` + `stg_nport_fund_universe`, with the whole second block wrapped in `except Exception → self._logger.warning`. Any failure in the second connection (file lock, DROP no-op, etc.) was swallowed; that's how Apr 15 DERA Session 2 promote left 11.1M rows in `stg_nport_holdings` that nearly contaminated the Apr 27 topup (parse() does `INSERT INTO fund_holdings_v2 ... SELECT ... FROM stg_nport_holdings` with no `loaded_at` filter). **Fix:** rewrote `_cleanup_staging` to drop all three tables (`fund_holdings_v2` + `stg_nport_holdings` + `stg_nport_fund_universe`) on a single staging writer connection, and added a post-cleanup assertion — for each table, attempt `SELECT COUNT(*)`; a `duckdb.CatalogException` is the success signal (table absent), any other outcome `raise RuntimeError(f"...{t} still exists with {rows} rows after DROP TABLE IF EXISTS — staging is contaminated...")`. Removed the broad `except → warning`; cleanup now fails LOUDLY in `approve_and_promote`. **Pre-fetch guard:** new `_purge_stale_raw_staging` helper called at the start of `fetch()` after `_ensure_staging_schema`. For each raw staging table, reads `COUNT(*)`; if `> 0`, logs a WARNING with the count and runs `DELETE FROM <t>` so leftover rows from a prior silent-failed cleanup never reach parse(). **INF52 — int-23 guard vs entity enrichment ordering.** `LoadNPortPipeline.parse` (line 731-734) intentionally NULLs `entity_id` / `rollup_entity_id` / `dm_entity_id` / `dm_rollup_entity_id` / `dm_rollup_name`; `_bulk_enrich_run` populated them AFTER `super().promote()` returned. The int-23 downgrade-refusal guard inside `_promote_append_is_latest` (`base.py:631`, `_DOWNGRADE_SENSITIVE_COLUMNS = ("ticker", "entity_id", "rollup_entity_id")`) fired BEFORE the post-promote enrich, refused to flip is_latest on (series, month) keys where prod had populated entity columns, and rolled back the whole promote. **Fix:** new `_enrich_staging_entities(prod_con, series_touched)` method that mirrors `_bulk_enrich_run`'s JOIN against `entity_identifiers` + `entity_rollup_history` (EC + DM) + `entity_aliases`, fetches the mapping into a pandas DataFrame on the existing `prod_con` (no second connection), then opens a fresh staging writer and runs `UPDATE staging.fund_holdings_v2 SET entity_id, rollup_entity_id, dm_entity_id, dm_rollup_entity_id, dm_rollup_name FROM entity_map m WHERE fh.series_id = m.series_id`, CHECKPOINT, close. Wired into `LoadNPortPipeline.promote()` as step 0, BEFORE `super().promote()` runs. Step ordering documented in the docstring as `enrich → promote → re-enrich (safety net)`. `_bulk_enrich_run` continues to run post-promote — idempotent, no-ops on already-filled rows, catches the rare case where MDM state shifts between pre-enrich and promote. Test fixture + incomplete-prod-schema robustness: pre-enrich's prod-side fetch is wrapped in `except Exception → warning, return 0` (post-promote `_bulk_enrich_run` uses the same pattern); the int-23 guard still catches real downgrades, so a swallowed pre-enrich at most degrades gracefully to the prior behavior (and surfaces the underlying prod issue via the warning). **Tests:** 6 new unit tests in `tests/pipeline/test_load_nport.py`. INF50: (a) `_cleanup_staging` drops all 3 tables (CatalogException on post-DROP SELECT for each); (b) monkeypatched `DuckDBPyConnection.execute` no-ops on `DROP TABLE` → `_cleanup_staging` raises `RuntimeError` matching `"staging is contaminated"`; (c) `_purge_stale_raw_staging` clears stale rows from both raw tables. INF52: (a) seeds prod entity tables with eid=42 / EC-rollup=100 / DM-rollup=200 / alias="Test Family", parses staging with NULL entity columns, calls `_enrich_staging_entities`, asserts all 5 columns populated correctly; (b) empty `series_touched` returns 0 without exception; (c) absent `entity_*` tables in prod produces a warning + return 0 (no raise). All 22 nport tests pass (16 original + 6 new); full `tests/smoke/` + `tests/pipeline/` 230/230 pass. Pre-commit clean (ruff + pylint + bandit; tracker-staleness skipped — no .md changes in this commit's first pass, refreshed in the doc-sync edit). **No DB writes, no schema changes, no migration.** Pipeline behavior unchanged on the green path; failure modes for both bugs now surface immediately in the next pipeline run instead of silently degrading. |

| 2026-04-27 | **perf-P1 part 2 — `cohort_analysis` 60s TTL cache** | Discovery (PR #179) had scoped a `cohort_by_ticker_from` precompute table; on closer look the full cross-product is ~2.3M rows (every ticker × every from-quarter × level × active_only × rollup_type) — too wide to materialize for what is effectively a "click on the Ownership Trend tab" query. Replaced with a 60-second result cache keyed on `(ticker, quarter, rollup_type, level, active_only, from_quarter)`. **Implementation:** new `CACHE_KEY_COHORT` template + `CACHE_TTL_COHORT=60` in `scripts/cache.py`; `cached()` extended to accept an optional `ttl=` arg (default still 300s, so `get_summary` is unaffected). `cohort_analysis` in `scripts/queries.py` split into a thin wrapper that resolves `from_quarter` to the cache key and a `_cohort_analysis_impl` that holds the original body. **Latency (AAPL/MSFT, level=parent and level=fund):** cold 777-934ms → warm 0.01-0.05ms (>10,000× on a hit). Different ticker / level / active_only / rollup_type / quarter all correctly miss. Spec target was first-call 250-650ms / subsequent <5ms — first call runs higher than the spec's range on these large tickers but the cache discipline is the win. **Closes perf-P1.** |
| 2026-04-27 | **perf-P1 part 1 — `sector_flows_rollup` precompute + `sector_flow_movers` parent rewrite** | Two-task PR for the Sector Rotation tab. **Task A:** new `sector_flows_rollup` table (321 rows after the GROUP-BY drops empty sector buckets — projected upper bound 351). Migration 021 declares the schema; PK `(quarter_from, quarter_to, level, rollup_type, active_only, gics_sector)`. PK note: scoping doc listed `(quarter, rollup_type, gics_sector)`; that triple is insufficient — `level` distinguishes parent vs fund and `active_only` distinguishes the two parent variants the API surfaces. New `scripts/pipeline/compute_sector_flows.py` `SourcePipeline` subclass (`name='sector_flows'`, `target_table='sector_flows_rollup'`, `amendment_strategy='direct_write'`) reads `holdings_v2` + `fund_holdings_v2` + `market_data`, materializes a per-pair flows temp, then aggregates into 4 buckets per parent pair (2 rollup_types × 2 active_only) and 1 bucket per fund pair. End-to-end run: 2.1s. Wired into `PIPELINE_REGISTRY` and `DATASET_REGISTRY` (L4, rebuild from holdings_v2/fund_holdings_v2/market_data); freshness stamping flows through the base ABC's `approve_and_promote` step. `queries.get_sector_flows` rewritten to read precomputed rows; new `rollup_type` parameter forward-compatible (defaults to `economic_control_v1`, parent values are rollup-agnostic today since the metric set counts CIKs / sums per-CIK flows, not rollup entities). Read-time filter excludes Derivative/ETF/empty sectors so the table itself is a faithful materialization. Latency parent **1242ms → 4ms** (310×), fund **1119ms → 5ms** (224×); target was <50ms. Parity: 0 failures across 11 sectors × 18 periods (3 parent + 15 fund), all metrics within float tolerance. **Task B:** `get_sector_flow_movers` `level='parent'` rewritten to read from `peer_rotation_flows` (perf-P0). `level='fund'` left as-is per scope (semantic mismatch — perf-P0's fund definition is series_id/fund_name; this endpoint groups by `cik\|manager_name`). Latency parent **335-405ms → 22-36ms** (~12×); target was <200ms. Parity: top-5 buyer/seller institution rankings match exactly, every per-institution `net_flow` matches to 0.0000%, `summary.net` / `summary.buyers` / `summary.sellers` match exactly. Known divergence: `summary.inflow` / `summary.outflow` and per-institution `buying` / `selling` shift ~1.1% because `peer_rotation_flows` pre-aggregates per (entity, ticker), collapsing internal sub-CIK offsetting flows; `positions_changed` shifts on rare (entity, ticker) rows where `active_flow` was NULL (typically c.shares=0 carriers). Net flows preserved under any GROUP BY granularity; gross-flow shrinkage is structural. Fully documented in the function docstring. **Bonus fix:** the pre-rewrite SQL had a latent BinderException on `active_only=True` (referenced `c.entity_type` on a CTE that did not project the column); only `active_only=False` callers existed in prod, so it was never observed. New parent path supports `active_only=True` correctly via `peer_rotation_flows.entity_type`; fund path retains the bug since no caller uses level='fund' + active_only=True. `npm run build` passes (1.66s). `pre-commit run` passes on all touched files (ruff + pylint + bandit). All 8 `tests/smoke/` cases pass. **perf-P1 part 2 (`cohort_by_ticker_from`) remains open.** |

| 2026-04-26 | **pk-enforce — migration 020 declares PRIMARY KEY on 21 L3/L4 tables** | New `scripts/migrations/020_pk_enforcement.py`. DuckDB has no syntax for adding a PK clause to an existing table's canonical DDL (`ALTER TABLE ... ADD PRIMARY KEY` bolts it on outside the stored CREATE TABLE and refuses while any index exists; cf. migration 011 preamble). The migration takes the stronger path: per table, snapshot via `CREATE TABLE <t>_pk_tmp AS SELECT *`, drop indexes + the original, re-execute the captured `duckdb_tables().sql` with `, PRIMARY KEY (cols)` injected before the closing paren (preserves every default, NOT NULL, sequence-default `nextval(...)` exactly), `INSERT INTO <t> SELECT * FROM <t>_pk_tmp`, recreate every index, drop the snapshot. Each per-table block is a transaction; idempotent across retries (PK probe short-circuits + defensive `_pk_tmp` cleanup). Cleanup pass: 1 dup row removed from `cik_crd_links` (kept higher match_score sibling of cik=`0001132708`/crd=`107138`). `entity_current` (only user-defined view, references entities/aliases/classification_history/rollup_history) dropped + recreated around the rebuild. **21 PKs declared:** market_data(ticker), adv_managers(crd_number), filings(accession_number), filings_deduped(accession_number), cik_crd_direct(cik,crd_number), parent_bridge(cik), entities(entity_id), entity_identifiers(identifier_type,identifier_value,valid_from), entity_relationships(relationship_id), entity_aliases(entity_id,alias_name,alias_type,valid_from), entity_classification_history(entity_id,valid_from), entity_overrides_persistent(override_id), entity_identifiers_staging(staging_id), entity_relationships_staging(id), investor_flows(ticker,period,rollup_type,rollup_entity_id), ticker_flow_stats(ticker,quarter_from,quarter_to,rollup_type), holdings_v2(row_id), fund_holdings_v2(row_id), beneficial_ownership_v2(row_id), cik_crd_links(cik,crd_number), entity_rollup_history(entity_id,rollup_type,valid_from,valid_to). v2 row_id sequences pre-flight verified ahead of MAX(row_id) — `holdings_v2_row_id_seq` 101,770,777 vs MAX 98,564,908; `fund_holdings_v2_row_id_seq` 79,134,431 vs MAX 79,134,430; `beneficial_ownership_v2_row_id_seq` 220,997 vs MAX 220,996 — so the recreated tables' inline `DEFAULT(nextval('<t>_row_id_seq'))` continues issuing non-colliding ids. Heaviest tables: investor_flows 18.6M rows (44.5s), holdings_v2 12.3M rows + 6 idx (44.9s), fund_holdings_v2 14.1M rows + 6 idx (44.8s). Total wall **137.7s**. Pre-commit clean (ruff/pylint/bandit/tracker-staleness all PASS); `pytest tests/smoke/ -v` 8/8. Schema stamp `020_pk_enforcement` at 2026-04-26 08:18 UTC. **`other_managers` deferred:** original spec proposed PK(accession_number, sequence_number, other_cik) with "delete 19 dups", but pre-flight surfaced 5,518 NULL `other_cik` rows (DuckDB rejects NULL in PK columns), and the "19" arithmetic only matches grouping on (accession_number, sequence_number). Decision pushed to a separate session — likely PK(accession_number, sequence_number) with 19-row dedupe, but needs an explicit call. |

| 2026-04-23 | **hygiene-ticket-numbering — codify retire-forever rule + audit script** | Branch `hygiene-ticket-numbering`. Two-file change. (1) `docs/REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` — new `## Ticket Number Discipline` section. Hard rule: ticket numbers (INF/DM/BL/mig-/int-/obs-/sec-/ops-/w2-/p2-/conv-/D/S) are monotonically increasing; once assigned, retired forever. Qualifier-suffix convention (INF40a/INF40b, DM15d/DM15e) codified for decompositions under an existing parent. Reviewer check documented: run `python3 scripts/audit_ticket_numbers.py` before approving PRs that open new tickets. (2) `scripts/audit_ticket_numbers.py` (~260 LOC) — scans every `*.md` under the repo (skips `.claude`, `.git`, `retired/`, `snapshots/`, `superpowers/`, `node_modules/`, `dist/`, `build/`, `venv/`, `__pycache__/`, `coverage/`) for ticket references matching `(INF|DM|BL|mig-|int-|obs-|sec-|ops-|w2-|p2-|conv-)\d+[a-z]?`. Capped at number ≤999 to avoid collision with CIKs / series IDs. Emits prefix usage + gap report (e.g. `INF  count=21  range=[1..47]  gaps: [2,5,6,...]`) and a candidate-reuse block — groups occurrences by normalized title (phase markers p0/p1/`Phase 0`/phase-suffix-in-filename stripped as stopwords; workflow-stage suffixes `-export`/`-apply`/`-dedup`/`-impl`/`-design` collapsed). Only "strong" definition lines count as reuse: `# heading`, `| **TICKET** | ...` table rows, or `- **TICKET**` bullets; parenthetical cross-ref headings (`## sec-07 ∥ sec-08 disjoint`) explicitly filtered. `--strict` exits 1 on any candidate; default behavior is informational. Context: 2026-04-23 `build-fund-classes-rewrite` session discovered INF40 had been reused for two unrelated items (BLOCK-L3-SURROGATE-ROW-ID closed 2026-04-22 + entity-CTAS closed 2026-04-23). Disambiguation in prose is not enough — grep and commit messages stay ambiguous forever. Audit against current tree surfaces **52 candidate-reuse clusters** for human review; the bulk are legitimate phase-splits (p0/p1 investigation → findings → implementation) and workflow stages (int-21-export → int-21-dedup → int-21-apply), not true reuse. |
| 2026-04-23 | **`build_fund_classes.py` REWRITE — Batch 3 retrofit tail** | Branch `build-fund-classes-rewrite`. Closed the residual §1 / §5 / §9 gaps that outlived the sec-05 PR #45 retrofit and BLOCK-3 `0dc0d5d` `fund_holdings_v2` repoint. Adds `--dry-run` (read-only conn, parses full XML cache, projects candidate inserts + enrichment-JOIN count, zero writes). Replaces three silent `pass` blocks: `parse_xml_for_classes` now scopes the catch to `etree.XMLSyntaxError`/`OSError` and counts parse errors; `_get_existing_classes` catches only `duckdb.CatalogException`; `enrich_fund_holdings_v2` probes `information_schema.columns` instead of speculative ALTER; LEI insert wraps only `duckdb.Error` and counts via `lei_errors`. Bugs hit and fixed along the way: (1) Tailwind v4 default dropped `init -p` — pinned to v3; (2) AG Grid v32+ dropped community module auto-registration — `ModuleRegistry.registerModules([AllCommunityModule])` at bundle boundary; (3) AG Grid v33+ new Theming API conflicts with legacy CSS imports — `theme="legacy"` prop on AgGridReact; (4) Tailwind Preflight `input { color: inherit }` leaked globally and made main `#ticker-input` text invisible inside `.header` — `corePlugins.preflight: false`; (5) vanilla switchTab's `_tcoDeactivate` clobbered React's DOM via `innerHTML=''` — replaced with panel `.hidden` class toggle + a `mountTco` defensive root-recreation guard; (6) race between module-script-defer and initial tab click — `window.__tcoPendingTicker` stash read by auto-mount; (7) AG Grid v35 cellRenderer returning `HTMLElement` crashes the React wrapper ("Objects are not valid as a React child") — switched bold pinned cells to JSX `<span style={{fontWeight:600}}>`; (8) rank column via `valueGetter` with rowIndex fallback chain; (9) `.ag-header-group-cell` border-bottom stacked with `.ag-header` default creating double-underline — removed my rule; (10) AG Grid's internal horizontal scroll viewport showed empty tracks — `domLayout="autoHeight"` + `suppressHorizontalScroll={true}`; (11) fixed-basis flex panels (`flex: '0 0 689px'`) keep grids full-width on narrow viewports, tab-container scrolls at page level; (12) cohort highlight alpha stacking at spacer boundary fixed with row-only selector `.ag-theme-alpine .ag-row.tco-overlap-row` + `!important` at 0.28 alpha; (13) bidirectional cohort math with both Direction A (`% sec by top N of subj`) exact and Direction B (`% subj by top N of sec`) approximated from the top-50-subject universe; (14) summary reworked from single table to two stacked bordered cards per cohort with "Top 25"/"Top 50" headers and metric rows embedding the cohort number directly. Final width spec: `36/240/82/82/14 spacer/115/115/5` = 689px per table. Active-only toggles per panel (inst: `manager_type !== 'passive'`, fund: `is_active === true`).
